  <a href="/user/show/1390765-diane" class="left imgcol" title="Diane"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1296562176p2/1390765.jpg" alt="Diane" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/379181241?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 28, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1390765-diane" class="user" title="Diane">Diane</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/376630.Snow_Angels" title="Paperback 9780312422769" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1390765-diane?shelf=audio-books-read" class="actionLinkLite">audio-books-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer379181241">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14390417543206685874"> Snow Angels, was a very dark novel of small town life in Pennsylvania in the mid-1970s. It's a tragic story that involves two families, and as the tragedy is introduced early on the story then flashes back so that the reader gets the full picture of events leading up to the tragedy.<br /><br />In the story, Arthur Parkinson, now a grown man returns to his childhood community in PA, where he reflects on the events which attributed to his unhappy childhood. His parents were not nurturing parents, rather self</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14390417543206685874"> Snow Angels, was a very dark novel of small town life in Pennsylvania in the mid-1970s. It's a tragic story that involves two families, and as the tragedy is introduced early on the story then flashes back so that the reader gets the full picture of events leading up to the tragedy.<br /><br />In the story, Arthur Parkinson, now a grown man returns to his childhood community in PA, where he reflects on the events which attributed to his unhappy childhood. His parents were not nurturing parents, rather selfish and self-centered. After some irresponsible acts, their marriage dissolves, and 15 year-old Arthur now moves with his mother to a rundown apartment. He becomes aloof, and he copes by smoking pot, listening to loud music and pretending not to care, about his new situation or the lives his parents are now leading.<br /><br />The other story involves Arthur's former babysitter, Annie Marchand, another selfish, self-centered woman, who puts her own desires ahead of her daughter Tara. She leaves her husband, a man who soon begins to lose his grip and spirals out of control.<br /><br />Without giving away too much of this short novel, I must say that I found all of the characters, with the exception of Arthur, to be their own worst enemies. I felt for Arthur, as his life growing up was what it was because of the irresponsible acts of those who were responsible for him. Although this was not a favorite O'Nan book of mine, it's probably the most depressing of any that I've read or listened to, it was still a good story. This is one book that I DO NOT recommend listening to the audio. Although the reader was good, the tone made the story seem all the more bleak.<br /><br />3.5/5 stars</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14390417543206685874">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_86166666">

  <a href="/user/show/2207055-kari" class="left imgcol" title="kari"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1262446392p2/2207055.jpg" alt="kari" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/86166666?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 01, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2207055-kari" class="user" title="kari">kari</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/376630.Snow_Angels" title="Paperback 9780312422769" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2207055-kari?shelf=2010" class="actionLinkLite">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer86166666">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13237351422695903193">This one I read as an example of dark fiction and I'm not sure exactly what the point of it all is.<br />The story is definitely dark. <br />A teenage boy, Artie, is caught in the middle of his parent's divorce. He often gets high with his best friend as a way of dealing with their constant fighting and, after the separation, his mother's anger and dependence on him. Artie's mother seems to take her aggression out on him and I never understood exactly what she was so angry about since it was her actions tha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13237351422695903193">This one I read as an example of dark fiction and I'm not sure exactly what the point of it all is.<br />The story is definitely dark. <br />A teenage boy, Artie, is caught in the middle of his parent's divorce. He often gets high with his best friend as a way of dealing with their constant fighting and, after the separation, his mother's anger and dependence on him. Artie's mother seems to take her aggression out on him and I never understood exactly what she was so angry about since it was her actions that brought on the divorce. His chapters of the book are told in first person past tense. I'm not sure why a page or two of him as an adult were included as it added nothing to the story as far as understanding how this affected his life as an adult. <br />The other chapters are told in third person present. Annie, a young woman who years ago had been Artie's occasional babysitter is murdered and you find out who did it and why and what leads up to it. It is very creepy being in the mind of her killer as he justifies what he plans to do and the story is terribly sad. <br />One of the things that bothered me most is there was no resolution of any kind for the teenage boy; the story simply ends.<br />The book is well written, with clear voices and even with the different view points, it was easy to understand. Although some of the phrasing and thoughts I had to read over a few times before I could understand exactly what was going on. It tends to jump right into a character's thoughts without knowing exactly what's going on. <br />This will be the last dark literature I read. Unless you want to really depress yourself, don't pick this one up.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13237351422695903193">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NNiUv3/UKdOjJX70NYvDbzx0Jm71VRz9bN5tgnT73oZRDKtsjQY9KS/9Ck9L6iXddYPld7yIW1cG12gQuG4oww==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/OrvFDP3NGlpyNEPrQWr4iKcfNdsIict7VIRgAfQ08mZPtDHwSUgk+UQpbTTZE1Qa2u/ziX/YIeHWxQSy0UljA==')})

The Poet of Tolstoy Park is the unforgettable novel based&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText17675692150115119426\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;“The more you transform your life from the material to the spiritual domain, the less you become afraid of death.” Leo Tolstoy spoke these words, and they became Henry Stuart’s raison d’etre. The Poet of Tolstoy Park is the unforgettable novel based on the true story of Henry Stuart’s life, which was reclaimed from his doctor’s belief that he would not live another year.Henry responds to the news by slogging home barefoot in the rain. It’s 1925. The place: Canyon County, Idaho. Henry is sixty-seven, a retired professor and a widower who has been told a warmer climate would make the end more tolerable. San Diego would be a good choice. Instead, Henry chose Fairhope, Alabama, a town with utopian ideals and a haven for strong-minded individualists. Upton Sinclair, Sherwood Anderson, and Clarence Darrow were among its inhabitants. Henry bought his own ten acres of piney woods outside Fairhope. Before dying, underscored by the writings of his beloved Tolstoy, Henry could begin to “perfect the soul awarded him” and rest in the faith that he, and all people, would succeed, “even if it took eons.” Human existence, Henry believed, continues in a perfect circle unmarred by flaws of personality, irrespective of blood and possessions and rank, and separate from organized religion. In Alabama, until his final breath, he would chase these high ideas.But first, Henry had to answer up for leaving Idaho. Henry’s dearest friend and intellectual sparring partner, Pastor Will Webb, and Henry’s two adult sons, Thomas and Harvey, were baffled and angry that he would abandon them and move to the Deep South, living in a barn there while he built a round house of handmade concrete blocks. His new neighbors were perplexed by his eccentric behavior as well. On the coldest day of winter he was barefoot, a philosopher and poet with ideas and words to share with anyone who would listen. And, mysteriously, his “last few months” became years. He had gone looking for a place to learn lessons in dying, and, studiously advanced to claim a vigorous new life.The Poet of Tolstoy Park is a moving and irresistible story, a guidebook of the mind and spirit that lays hold of the heart. Henry Stuart points the way through life’s puzzles for all of us, becoming in this timeless tale a character of such dimension that he seems more alive now than ever.From the Hardcover     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18341.Stewart_O_Nan">About Stewart O'Nan</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/18341.Stewart_O_Nan"><img alt="18341" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1206592605p2/18341.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer16394100667883609553">Stewart O'Nan is the author of eleven novels, including Snow Angels and A Prayer for the Dying, a story collection, and two works of nonfiction. His previous novel, Last Night at the Lobster, was a national bestseller, was nominated for the Los Angeles Times Book Prize, and was named one of the New York Public Library Books to Remember. Additionally, Granta named him one of the 20 Best Young Ameri</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16394100667883609553">Stewart O'Nan is the author of eleven novels, including Snow Angels and A Prayer for the Dying, a story collection, and two works of nonfiction. His previous novel, Last Night at the Lobster, was a national bestseller, was nominated for the Los Angeles Times Book Prize, and was named one of the New York Public Library Books to Remember. Additionally, Granta named him one of the 20 Best Young American Novelists. O'Nan lives with his family in Avon, Connecticut."<br /><br />Note: Stewart O'Nan published also the book "A Good Day to Die" under his pseudonym James Coltrane. You'll find it here: <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5445945.James_Coltrane_Stewart_O_Nan_">http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5445945.James_Coltrane_Stewart_O_Nan_<br /></a><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16394100667883609553">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/18341.Stewart_O_Nan" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Stewart O'Nan...</a>
